  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_5b45752b-a551-4b54-abfd-13fe7e7bebc1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

  <span id="freeText5905910471105621223" style="display:none"><i>Powerful love comes with a price. Who will be the sacrifice?</i><br /><br />Kami has lost the boy she loves, is tied to a boy she does not, and faces an enemy more powerful than ever before. With Jared missing for months and presumed dead, Kami must rely on her new magical link with Ash for the strength to face the evil spreading through her town.<br /><br />Rob Lynburn is now the master of Sorry-in-the-Vale, and he demands a death. Kami will use every tool at her disposal to stop him. Together with Rusty, Angela, and Holly, she uncovers a secret that might be the key to saving the town. But with knowledge comes responsibility—and a painful choice. A choice that will risk not only Kami’s life, but also the lives of those she loves most.<br /><br />This final book in the <i>Lynburn Legacy</i> is a wild, entertaining ride from beginning to shocking end.</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Straight up? No reason at all. Honest to god. <br/> The only reason that makes sense is that the people in this book are idiots with no sense of self prese<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Straight up? No reason at all. Honest to god. <br /> The only reason that makes sense is that the people in this book are idiots with no sense of self preservation. That includes the main characters. Because when magical sorcerers threaten to murder people in your town, smart rational people gtfo. No one in this book did that, i.e. no one in this book has sense.<br /> Or maybe no one owns a car, who knows. *shrugs*<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8859363541314742138">So, how perfect was it that I had The Civil Wars - "Talking In Your Sleep" playing on repeat the <i>entire</i> time I read this? Sigh. Swoon.<br/><br/>SRB did it again. <br/>And I regret nothing. <br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411609856ra/11255413.gif' width='500' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410480453ra/11112970.gif' width='500' height='270' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I waited a year for this book. Clearly, I had high expectations. <br/>This book did not exceed my expectations, but met them. Thoroughly. <br/>Again, I regret nothing.<br/><br/>My emotions are all warped and messy, but I’ll *try* to make this review clean, short, and to the point.<br/> <br/>The epic conclusion to Kami and Jared’s explosive, tumultuous, s</span>
  <span id="freeText8859363541314742138" style="display:none">So, how perfect was it that I had The Civil Wars - "Talking In Your Sleep" playing on repeat the <i>entire</i> time I read this? Sigh. Swoon.<br><br>SRB did it again. <br>And I regret nothing. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411609856ra/11255413.gif" width="500" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1410480453ra/11112970.gif" width="500" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I waited a year for this book. Clearly, I had high expectations. <br>This book did not exceed my expectations, but met them. Thoroughly. <br>Again, I regret nothing.<br><br>My emotions are all warped and messy, but I’ll *try* to make this review clean, short, and to the point.<br> <br>The epic conclusion to Kami and Jared’s explosive, tumultuous, smoldering love was well played. <b>Their drama did drag, but it had to.</b> I eagerly welcomed that familiar slow burn of ‘almost-but-not-quite’ fiery-passionate, love/tension/banter/chemistry between the two. Their “end-game” or shall I say, “fresh start” was predictable, but right. It couldn’t have ended any other way. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411609856ra/11255414.gif" width="500" height="267" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The humor was spot-on.</b> I think that’s the hardest part of writing. Not everyone has the same sense of humor, and it’s hard throwing in the not-so-subtle jokes around in every other paragraph or two. But, SRB did it with such finesse! <b>Awesomely played, and maddeningly hilarious.</b> Like, who does that? In the midst of serious life-and-death issues – and even when there <i>was</i> <b>an unfortunate and utterly heartbreaking death of a beloved character (a favorite of mine),</b> I (guilty) gave in to the treacherous laughter that overcame me with Kami’s quick witted one-liners. Of course, I wanted there to be a bit more mourning on that beloved characters’ behalf, but whatever. <i>Minor issue. </i> <b>My point being: the 'humor' didn't cheapen the overall story for me. It enhanced it. </b><br><br>On the other hand, while Ash was somewhat of a disappointment in UNTOLD, and though he didn’t fully redeem himself, I didn’t mind. <b>He was always meant to play that secondary role, but he did it well. </b>This time around, he shone in his role. <br><br>I loved the <b>familial relationships</b> in this story – everyone came together throughout it all. So maybe I missed a really epic battle. Maybe I thought the Big Fight would’ve been dragged out a bit more, and the ending a bit more explosive and just harder overall. <br><br>Maybe I didn’t think everyone would make it out alive – so safe – with all their limbs attached. Some didn’t, but I can admit that there wasn’t much of a clash. Not much of a battle. But there was a fight. <b>Each character in their own way, fought to overcome their weaknesses. </b>Again, if you want to take it all literally and only determine the scale of the 'war' in a purely physical or magical matter, it was <b>somewhat anticlimactic,</b> but again, the familial relationships, friendships, and secondary romances made up for all that. Not to mention, the internal battles they each faced. With tremendous bravery. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411609856ra/11255415.gif" width="300" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The first two books were incredibly dark and I loved that. This book was <i>much fluffier</i> in comparison, but I didn't mind. Often times, you see characters <b>starting off all care-free and happy and innocent, and then the book shifts with danger and heartbreak and everything else</b> threatening to take that away. This series kind of went in "reverse" and it felt right. <br><br>I think... I wanted more angst, drama, heartbreak, revenge, blood and more development overall for Rob's character and his relationship to both Ash and Jared. On that note, I really felt a bit shafted. But I guess the story was never <i>really</i> about those relationships anyway. And, what's the point of cultivating those relationships only to burn them down? <br><br>All in all, despite the aforementioned underwhelming portions of the story – I wouldn’t have wanted it any other way.<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1411609856ra/11255416.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
<b><i> <br>“You always thought Holly was great.” <br><br>“She is great,” said Jared. <br><br>“And beautiful. She’s like a star to me, something bright and lovely seen from another world. She’s someone else’s sun. That’s how all other girls are to me. You’re my sun.” <br><br>It was a nice recovery.<br><br>“Your courtship method of arrogance, self-loathing, and then telling me how beautiful other girls are is pretty unique,” said Kami. “I like it..."<br></i></b><br> </blockquote><br><br>5 shiny stars, all the way. #TEAMJARED4EVER<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1406275873ra/10528851.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8859363541314742138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_716285178" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/716285178" />
    <a title="Susana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7301000-susana"><img alt="Susana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483821488p2/7301000.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/716285178?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susana" href="/user/show/7301000-susana">Susana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=2014">2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=drama-drama-drama">drama-drama-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=love-triangle-mess">love-triangle-mess</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=tstlc">tstlc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=just-no">just-no</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer716285178" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13411537331675599078">Almost five o'clock in the morning...so I am not sure...3 stars?<br/>2 stars?<br/>________________<br/>And this is how you wreck a perfectly amazing series.<br/><br/><a href='http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/> <b>How to wreck an amazing series: A recipe for Disaster</b><br/><br/> Leave a love triangle simmering in a tasteless broth. When it looks as if <b>the thing</b> may not have a single reason to exist, <u>turn the power up</u> all over again!<br/><br/>Insert about 20% cringe worthy jokes so that it may help downplay all the emotional drama happening.<br/><br/> Add close to none character development, so</span>
  <span id="freeText13411537331675599078" style="display:none">Almost five o'clock in the morning...so I am not sure...3 stars?<br>2 stars?<br>________________<br>And this is how you wreck a perfectly amazing series.<br><br><a href="http://paperbackwonderland.blogspot.pt/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380238999i/681674.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br> <b>How to wreck an amazing series: A recipe for Disaster</b><br><br> Leave a love triangle simmering in a tasteless broth. When it looks as if <b>the thing</b> may not have a single reason to exist, <u>turn the power up</u> all over again!<br><br>Insert about 20% cringe worthy jokes so that it may help downplay all the emotional drama happening.<br><br> Add close to none character development, so that the characters don't have to...I don't know?<br>Grow up?<br><br> Kill characters at discretion...you will determine when enough is enough _apparently never :/ _ by the cries of former devoted readers...<br><br> Angst, angst, and more angst....when in doubt add more.<br><br>Let the characters behave as idiots as much as possible, without no regard for logical reasoning...<br><br> Kill one of your favourite , FAVOURITE, character, in a move completely illogical (according to his personality) and very faith oriented...<br><br> Leave the readers _who are reading fantasy _ upset with the somewhat preachy tone of the thing...<br><br><i>"There were marks of pain on his face, but no anger and no fear. He looked a little sad."</i><br>(..)<br><br><i>He stayed like a shadow in every corner of our home, stayed a stain on our hearts. I felt it. I can’t believe that good will leave us when evil remains. I will not. I do not.”</i><br><br> ARGHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH!!!!<br><br> Some people will probably say:<br><br><i>"Oh, she's mad because ______ _______ was killed, so she's taking it out on the author and on the story."</i><br><br> <br><br>I am not.<br>And I am not mad...reading this, left me somewhat empty of emotions. .. I may think about it once in awhile, and question what possessed me to read this volume _ the fact that I loved the previous two volumes may have had something to do with it _ but I don't feel angry enough to be...screaming or ranting :/<br>I am just sad.<br><br> The beginning was good, and I was looking forward in seeing Jared being rescued.<br>Unfortunately after that, things went into a <u>carousel of ya "love triangle mess" angst fest</u> that was just _as other reviewers have mentioned it before _ prone to a lot of headesking.<br>The angst!<br>The idiocy!<br>The absence of a rational dialogue!<br><br>Yes, we all know that Jared is a special flower with whom we need to have a lot of patience dealing with, but c'mon!<br>No one's that stupid! And clueless!<br>And Ash?<br>Ash?<br><b>Who cares about Ash?</b><br><br> Between the number of things that I just couldn't understand are:<br><br>Jared is being held prisoner at Aurimere. His aunt who is a sorceress can cross the "magical" fire, and blend into the shadows...<br><br>SO WHY DIDN'T SHE TRIED TO FIND THE POOR GUY??<br><br> Also, you're caught in a town controlled by raging lunatics.<br>People are being killed as flies.<br>You have no power with which to fight the bad guy..what do you do?<br><br> <br><br>A) Try to leave the city as soon as possible<br><br>B) Make up another crazy plan that will probably end up with another person being killed..<br>Yes, Kami went with option B, which is only natural, because the story takes place in Sorry in The Vale.<br>BUT, I really think that the option A should at least have been mentioned as a possibility: maybe they were magically locked in there. Fine. <br>But at some point people, logical, sensible people, like I don't know...Rusty? Should have mentioned it....and at least tried to do something about it.<br><br> The statue scene...I found it too..."Disneylike" especially after what had happened with you know <b>whom</b>...<br><br>There where characters who were brought into the story apparently for only sacrificial purposes...<br>Kids who were being constantly kidnapped... <br>People kept crossing magical fires that no one should be able to cross..<br>Rescue attempts were done involving a great, great number of people: It was like seeing a bunch of tourists in a place where they shouldn't be.<br>Stealth, people!<br><br> The last part of the story, and all that happens _and not only that "specific killing" _ didn't work out for me.<br><br>The battle was....meh..<br><br> The relationship between Angela and Holly that was placed on hold for what felt like forever...and then dealt in a time and place, in which most readers probably didn't care about anything else at all.<br>And the last pages were really too lame to talk about.<br><br> A sad, and bloodthirsty story... yes.<br>Creepy and romantic, not really. Unless you're considering the definition of new adult's romance.<br><br> Best characters in the book?<br>Jon, Lillian ( I KNOW!!)...and Rusty.<br><br> <br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13411537331675599078" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=awful-love-interest">awful-love-interest</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1062911253" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer829736669631819555"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>This was a bit of a mixed bag, I did enjoy it overall but there were a lot of things that I wasn't impressed with - mainly the MC (Kami), her love life, the poor pacing and the rushed ending.<br/> <br/>-What's what: Evil Rob and his evil sorcerers have taken over Sorry-in-the-Vale. Naturally, Kami and the Scooby gang try to stop him. Also angst, teen romance, and more angst.<br/><br/>-Kami was such a judgemental, holier than thou, hypocrite. The way she looked down at the people who fought with the bad guys</span>
  <span id="freeText829736669631819555" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />This was a bit of a mixed bag, I did enjoy it overall but there were a lot of things that I wasn't impressed with - mainly the MC (Kami), her love life, the poor pacing and the rushed ending.<br /> <br />-What's what: Evil Rob and his evil sorcerers have taken over Sorry-in-the-Vale. Naturally, Kami and the Scooby gang try to stop him. Also angst, teen romance, and more angst.<br /><br />-Kami was such a judgemental, holier than thou, hypocrite. The way she looked down at the people who fought with the bad guys or the people who weren't fighting on any side because they were too afraid was beyond irritating. She had no compassion or understanding for them being scared or being unable to stand up for themselves, not everyone has the ability, powers or support to act all heroic.<br />It was also ridiculous how she judged Amber for hurting Jared yet it was perfectly okay for her to threaten, torture, and gang up on her. Amber had little choice in the matter, but that didn't matter, it was one rule for Kami and her friends and another for everyone else. The cow.<br /><br />-Jared was his usual prick self, he treated Kami like rubbish and was constantly hot and cold with her. After everything they went through I thought he would finally stop acting like a bratty child, but no he was just as bad as before. I guess, Kami and Jared were meant to be, they were both as bad as each other.<br /><br />-I loved Angela, Rusty, Martha, and Kami's family. They made the story so much more fun and interesting, they were the ones I rooted for and was invested in. I really hate that Rusty died though, he was the best and most worthy character, he should have been the last person to die. I would have much preferred Ash or Jared being killed off. <br /><br />-Angela's smackdown of Kami was great, Rusty's death was her fault, if she hadn't been such an interfering bossy cow he wouldn't have died. I hated that Angela forgave Kami, she didn't deserve it.<br /><br />-The friendship/family bonds between the various characters was one of the best elements, there definitely should have been more focus on that instead of the wishy-washy romantic relationships.<br /><br />-I didn't like Holly in the second book, she was such a cow. But in this one she was so much more tolerable and she made more sense as a character, I really liked how sweet and supportive she was to her friends. And her relationship with Angela was cute too, I still think Angela deserved better than her but I guess she'll do for now.<br /><br />-The showdown at the end was a little underwhelming but the whole community feel of it was pretty good.<br /><br />All in all, this was a fairly entertaining read. I did get tired of Kami/Jared's up and down relationship, there were also parts that really dragged, and the ending was a tad anti-climactic but I enjoyed most of the side characters, the setting and certain friendships/relationships.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="829736669631819555" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_928169643" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/928169643" />
    <a title="Katie Montgomery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5117242-katie-montgomery"><img alt="Katie Montgomery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1301535416p2/5117242.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/928169643?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katie Montgomery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katie Montgomery" href="/user/show/5117242-katie-montgomery">Katie Montgomery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer928169643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6070940156233412586">Reviewers who insist on criticizing Ms. Brennan's work for containing 'too many dumb jokes': I'm sorry, WHAT?<br/><br/>Internet, you and I have not always seen eye to eye, but THIS! To criticize the final novel in a Brennan trilogy as being too laden with silly jokes is like criticizing van Gogh for not having enough ears. You may not like that artist's choice, you might be all like, "G-dawg, put down the razor dude, because first off antibiotics aren't going to even be a thing for like another fifty year</span>
  <span id="freeText6070940156233412586" style="display:none">Reviewers who insist on criticizing Ms. Brennan's work for containing 'too many dumb jokes': I'm sorry, WHAT?<br /><br />Internet, you and I have not always seen eye to eye, but THIS! To criticize the final novel in a Brennan trilogy as being too laden with silly jokes is like criticizing van Gogh for not having enough ears. You may not like that artist's choice, you might be all like, "G-dawg, put down the razor dude, because first off antibiotics aren't going to even be a thing for like another fifty years and also, seriously, dude, you, like, BARELY have enough ears as it is." And van Gogh might be like, "I respect your concern, and also, shut your face, because ART." And you would have to be all like, "OK, Imma go get the towels then, and YOU are the one doing the mopping, mister. Also, nice star painting."<br /><br />My point here is, Internet, that artists with a signature style are going to create work in that style. That is kind of the point. And while you can choose not to read a book that is written in a style not to your taste, it is probably not logical of you to condemn the artist for writing consistently in that style.<br /><br />Also, and this is the question that really stumps me, dudes, if you didn't like dumb jokes, why did you read 3 novels full of dumb jokes in the first place? Life is too short, guys.<br /><br />In all fairness, though, Vincent, seriously, prostitutes do not like it when you give them ears. Just saying.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_790385640" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/790385640" />
    <a title="Lucy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4089617-lucy"><img alt="Lucy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358564977p2/4089617.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/790385640?book_show_action=true">Dec 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lucy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lucy" href="/user/show/4089617-lucy">Lucy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089617-lucy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089617-lucy?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089617-lucy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4089617-lucy?shelf=2014-releases">2014-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer790385640" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13480242669729654819">I had high expectations for the final instalment of Brennan’s <i>Lynburn Legacy</i> trilogy after devouring the first two books last autumn. <i>The Lynburn Legacy</i> started out strong with witty, proactive characters, a unique genre mashup, and a wonderfully complicated romantic side-plot. But unfortunately, while I still enjoyed reading <i>Unmade</i>, I was disappointed by the series’ conclusion.<br/><br/>Despite the sleepy English village setting, the <i>Lynburn Legacy</i> series has always felt a little Americanised. I’m usuall</span>
  <span id="freeText13480242669729654819" style="display:none">I had high expectations for the final instalment of Brennan’s <i>Lynburn Legacy</i> trilogy after devouring the first two books last autumn. <i>The Lynburn Legacy</i> started out strong with witty, proactive characters, a unique genre mashup, and a wonderfully complicated romantic side-plot. But unfortunately, while I still enjoyed reading <i>Unmade</i>, I was disappointed by the series’ conclusion.<br /><br />Despite the sleepy English village setting, the <i>Lynburn Legacy</i> series has always felt a little Americanised. I’m usually not fussy when it comes to Americanisms in Brit lit, and I didn’t have a problem with it in the first two books of the series. But several times in <i>Unmade</i>, Brennan’s characters use American words and phrases in contexts that English teenagers just wouldn’t use them (e.g. Kami uses the word <i>college</i> to mean university, not sixth form). It was jarringly out of character, and I can’t believe it wasn’t picked up on by Brennan’s British publishers.<br /><br />Brennan’s characters still shine, but their actions are limited thanks to the (confusingly vague) laws of Brennan’s magic. Our previously proactive heroes spend the majority of the book sitting around, counting down the days until the villain makes a move. Kami, introduced in <i>Unspoken</i> as a fiercely loyal friend with a finely-tuned sense of justice, makes several decisions I found inconsistent with her character. I couldn’t accept that the same girl who staunchly refused to bow down to Rob Lynburn would willingly put a friend’s life on the line when told that it was her only option.<br /><br />The relationship between Kami and Jared hits yet more roadblocks in this instalment, and I found their development (or lack of development) frustrating. The progress Kami and Jared made in <i>Untold</i> is all but forgotten in an attempt to drag their tension-filled on-again-off-again romance out until the very last page. As a result, none of the actual problems of their relationship are dealt with - rather than hash out their unhealthy co-dependence or their communication issues, Kami and Jared spend the majority of the book refusing to acknowledge the other’s feelings.<br /><br />Despite my criticisms, I did like parts of the book - particularly any moment involving Angela Montgomery or Kami’s father, Jon Glass. I’m still a casual fan of this series, and I absolutely recommend <i>Unspoken</i>, although I don’t think I’ll be re-reading <i>Unmade</i> any time soon.<br /><br /><b>Publisher:</b> Simon &amp; Schuster<br /><b>Rating:</b> 2 stars | ★★✰✰✰<br />Review cross-posted to <a href="http://paperbackd.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Paperback'd</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13480242669729654819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11055685328495155412" style="display:none">Disappointed. Pissed. Underwhelmed. What was that ending?!<br><br>What is up with all these horrible end-of-trilogy books this year? Then it started getting the rolling eyes and frustrated sighs, and can we PLEASE JUST MOVE ON FROM THE JOKES. We, the readers, along with the characters had to wait till a certain date for them to make their move. Too bad the waiting took 50% of the book and with it it's bad jokes and mood killing. <br><br>We get to DDay and WOW, JUST WOW. Can not believe THAT happened. I cried. Actual tears slid down my eyes.     <a title="Katy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4572741-katy"><img alt="Katy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365039295p2/4572741.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/946269913?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer946269913" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3886604474905607870">But why?!? The No. 1 reason for my rating? The unnecessary use of bad jokes - or rather, the overdoing of it. Now I've known Kami, Rusty and pretty much all of the characters at one time or another to crack a line here or there to lighten the mood or awkward moment. But geez, I felt the whole book was littered with bad jokes on every page. What's worse is that Brennan KNEW, and she would have a character acknowledge it in the text. No, if you're going to do it, go with the whole "Scary Movie" pa</span>
  <span id="freeText3886604474905607870" style="display:none">But why?!? The No. 1 reason for my rating? The unnecessary use of bad jokes - or rather, the overdoing of it. Now I've known Kami, Rusty and pretty much all of the characters at one time or another to crack a line here or there to lighten the mood or awkward moment. But geez, I felt the whole book was littered with bad jokes on every page. What's worse is that Brennan KNEW, and she would have a character acknowledge it in the text. No, if you're going to do it, go with the whole "Scary Movie" parody type of narrative and just run with it. Don't do it and make excuses along the way. It was very hard for me to take the book seriously, and I was irritated beyond my mind. I felt a good third or half of this book was wasted on bad jokes when all I wanted to do was get to the meat of the story.<br /><br />Having said that, it's a shame that I didn't like this book because the first book was quite enjoyable, even though I could never stand Kami. (See past reviews for no love lost.) Even without the constant use of bad jokes, I just don't think this book did justice to the start of the series.<br /><br />First thing's first, the romance. I'm not stupid. I know there's going to be more Jared-Kami drama before everyone lives happily ever after, that is if they all make it. I expected it. However, this book still had the constant back and forth, and after a while, I stopped caring whether or not they're going to end up together or not. And the pet names? Ewww! And she did with the bad jokes, Brennan had Kami acknowledge it. But did it stop her? Nope, and the pet names got more ridiculous along the way (oh, yes, Kami says this herself in the book). Brennan did explain later, at least in Jared's point of view, why she wrote it that way, but it wasn't a good reason. Leave it out.<br /><br />As for the story, it was okay. You have your relationship drama (couple ones yes, but also family and friendships), digging into the past, problem solving to see why Rob is doing this and what he's after, a few action scenes and the big climax near the end. Parts were exciting enough and others were meh.<br /><br />And let me tell you I am devastated with the fate of my favorite character. That person was basically the only character I really liked and had always liked.<br /><br />I did feel that Elinor's story was really interesting. And it correlated enough to our trio, but I was unsatisfied that Brennan hadn't taken more advantage of the correlation. What I meant to say is I was just unsatisfied with what happened at the end. I felt the hero(one) of the story should have been someone else. Even though it's still somewhat cryptic, DO NOT CLICK UNTIL YOU'VE READ THIS BOOK. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I felt Jared deserved a showdown with Rob, after all that he has been through with (and without) this man. And especially since Elinor ended up with the most power and had survived. Sure history did not repeat itself, but it would have made more sense in my mind. Or if not, at least give that honor to Ash. He had been through a lot too, and after all, he was after linking with Kami, the most powerful sorcerer (sans Rob of course) at one time. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />And like I said, I have no love lost for Kami. There are plenty of no-nonsense, strong-minded, get-yourself-into-trouble-all-the-time characters that I admire while reading a book. Kami, I've just never been a fan of because of her annoying, self-righteous attitude. And I just felt throughout the series, there was just too much that revolved around her, when at the end of the day, she was just a source. Never understood it, but hey, that's just me.<br /><br />I'm sure a lot of other Lynburn Legacy fans would enjoy this book very much. For me, it was really, really, really hard to get past all the bad jokes because all I wanted to do was read the damn book, and another line was thrown at me. Honestly, if it weren't for them, I probably would have given this book 3 stars. Still, at the end of the day, I still haven't figured out what the "shocking end" part of the book was.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3886604474905607870" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1498936326" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498936326" />
    <a title="Julie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1143969-julie"><img alt="Julie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1409947508p2/1143969.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1498936326?book_show_action=true">Jan 06, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie" href="/user/show/1143969-julie">Julie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22009769-unmade">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=non-white-mc">non-white-mc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=parent-child-feelings">parent-child-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=sibling-feelings">sibling-feelings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=lgbtqa">lgbtqa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=witchcraft-and-wizardry">witchcraft-and-wizardry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1143969-julie?shelf=mixed-race">mixed-race</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1498936326" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5007717861708042406">I wanted to love this book, considering my investment in this series, but something was just off the whole way through. I was willing to be kind and give it 3 stars, but then the ending bumped it down another star -- I was tempted to almost go down as far as 1, but you have to really, <i>really</i> mess up to earn my withering scorn like that. Instead, I'm just left with the hefty power of my disappointment. Which also leaves me going: What's wrong with me? Was I just not in the mood for this book? But</span>
  <span id="freeText5007717861708042406" style="display:none">I wanted to love this book, considering my investment in this series, but something was just off the whole way through. I was willing to be kind and give it 3 stars, but then the ending bumped it down another star -- I was tempted to almost go down as far as 1, but you have to really, <i>really</i> mess up to earn my withering scorn like that. Instead, I'm just left with the hefty power of my disappointment. Which also leaves me going: What's wrong with me? Was I just not in the mood for this book? But I've been reading other YA fantasy with witches and things! I've been rolling around in shippy feelings over various books and movies! <i>What is wrong with me, or with this book?</i><br /><br />I loved <i>Unspoken</i>, you guys. So much. It was all feels and dark Gothic and a lurking mystery; plucky Nancy Drew heroines, two mysterious boys; the toxicity of a telepathic relationship. Then the sequel was mired with structural issues and the fact that nothing much happened at all. Now this. Maybe a 2+ year break was way too long for me to wait between books, but my structural problems from the second are still present here: time passes in a really vague, unclear manner, and there's still so much <i>waiting</i>. Plus, characters just randomly saunter right into the Evil Lair of Evil Sorcerers, and then the evil sorcerers saunter up to and attack their homes too, until I just don't understand why the heroes aren't dead yet.<br /><br />ALSO, Rob goes from an interestingly ambiguous character in the early books... to scenery-chomping, moustache-twirling, unrepentantly ~*evil*~, which is awful and tiresome. I like my villains more nuanced than this.<br /><br />I feel like Brennan had a good idea for a first book, a quiet lil mystery in a sleepily menacing Gothic town, with intense focus on interpersonal relationships -- but trying to expand it into a wide-spanning ~sorcerer's war~ just makes the narrative collapse under its own weight. What does it mean, to "rule" the town or to "destroy" it? <i>Why doesn't anyone talk about just leaving?</i> Why haven't the bad guys just outright killed our heroes already, considering they've repeatedly proven that they can reach them at any time? <i>Why don't the bad guys beef up their security measures more????</i> ("Rob Lynburn has always underestimated sources" is a thin, flimsy excuse.)<br /><br />Rescuing Jared felt easy; breaking in to steal Elinor's last clue felt easy; even going into the Crying Pools felt easy. The final conflict/climax is resolved within literally 1 page, which is the point where I went "Oh, hell no" and mentally docked one more star. Plus, as another reviewer has pointed out, I so heartily wish Ash or Jared had fought in the climax instead -- it was <i>their</i> family, and either or both of them deserved the shot to stand up to their own personal bogeyman.<br /><br />And I'm tired of three books seesawing with "will-they-won't-they" and introducing silly misunderstandings in order to keep Jared/Kami apart (if they would <i>just communicate!!!</i>). I think the YA ships that I'm more into are the ones where they do just go ahead and get together like reasonable people but then have to tackle real big shattering problems together; <i>or</i> they can't get together because there's a [war/dystopian revolution] to settle first, a la The Hunger Games. The whole 'WE'RE TOGETHER no wait we're not WE'RE TOGETHER wait no we can't be' drives me fucking crazy. It was drawn out until <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[literally the 99% marker, dragged out as long as humanly possible. I absolutely refuse. The wait didn't make me experience increased exultant joy over the resolution of the storyline; instead, the delayed gratification just made me feel tired of them by that point <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>.<br /><br />That said. The minor characters are <i>fantastic,</i> yet sadly underutilised: I wanted so much more of Angela/Holly, poor <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Henry Thornton <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is fridged, and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Rusty <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> is fridged. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I like that the male characters died to boost the female protag's development, but it felt quick and cursory and I didn't shed a single tear over Rusty, because... well, he was one of my favourites, so I don't know why I didn't feel anything. It was just all so many levels of convenient drama/melodrama. I felt more manipulated by the author, and thus angry, rather than heartbroken. I'm not in the "HOW DARE YOU DO THIS!?" camp reacting from emotion -- I've loved similar twists in other YA series, and burst out crying over them elsewhere -- but it just felt unnecessary and exploitative. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, man how much do I love Lillian the beautiful pristine robot. I almost wonder if she's autistic/has Aspergers, with her level of brilliance but inability to understand people's social norms.<br /><br />Looking at all of my favourite quotes below, I mostly loved the sassy quips, the humour, the found family of the Lynburns. Lillian and her boys were pretty much my favourite thing: Ash, the unfavourite, so desperate to be loved and needed; Jared, like an abused dog, slowly working his way back to trusting people and being okay with physical touch again. The book/series <i>is</i> wonderful for its depictions of recovery from abuse. The importance of community and family. The romance and sexiness of consent. Kami's issues being half-Japanese in a small, predominantly white town.<br /><br />But then it goes and has Ash be gross and overbearing and sexually pushy at Kami, when he is <i>telepathically tied to her</i>, so I really, truly can't believe that he would have behaved that way.<br /><br />Jared/Kami was a ship that used to make my heart do somersaults in the first book, but now I was just sick of them. Their melodrama is tired; they just don't <i>communicate</i>, are constantly misunderstanding each other and lashing out at each other, and it just does not feel like they make a healthy couple anymore. I don't like the 'inevitability' of their getting together because it smacks of their not having a choice. At the end, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kami 'rewards' him with resuming their telepathic link... when again, the whole point <i>to me</i> was that they had to learn to be without it, to love each other without it, to <i>choose</i> each other. Which, you could say that they did, that she tested him and made him admit that he loved her before revealing that she still had the link... but I don't like the idea that going forward, into the future, their relationship <i><b>has</b></i> to have this telepathy to function. (As it so clearly does, considering they DON'T TALK TO EACH OTHER and colossally misunderstand each other when they're not linked.) You have to be able to put up with a normal romantic relationship without this paranormal cheatsheet, y'all. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I love love love Ash and Rusty so much, though. I do like that the book addressed the what-if's of both these boys as romantic options -- but I am also a little tired of books where literally three different boys are head-over-heels for the protagonist. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ash's might have still come from his own emotional link to Jared, but that doesn't change the fact I had to sit through two scenes of boys flinging themselves at Kami &amp; being shot down, then her flinging herself at Jared &amp; being shot down. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Blergh. I don't know. I didn't <i>hate</i> it (hence 2 stars -- 'it was okay'), but my love for the first book and its potential means I just feel overwhelmingly irritated by how that potential has been squandered. If anyone has fix-it fic recommendations, I will take them. I think I'd like to see something where <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Ash and Kami do die, and Jared has to learn to live on his own and <i>for</i> himself. Or Kami gets together with Ash OR Rusty. Or Jared and Kami get together, but without the telepathy <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Pretty much literally anything <i>but</i> this ending, tbh.<br /><br /><b>In a nutshell</b>: Too much love triangle drama, messy plotting wrt the overarching conflict, too-neat resolutions, and a main ship that started off toxic in the first book and so I was fascinated to see how they rebuilt themselves, only to be annoyed that they never actually did.<br /><br />If you're going to start on this series: Read <i>Unspoken</i>, and then stop there.<br /><br />--<br /><br />Fave quotes:<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Kami wondered if she was a terrible girlfriend—if indeed she could be called a girlfriend, when it was basically a decision she’d come to entirely on her own—because she did not want to spend all her time gazing upon Jared as he slept.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “Of course I look different from all the other girls,” she said at last. “Anyone can see that. Half the town has suggested I date Raj Singh. Who’s thirteen.”<br />  Because being part Japanese was the same thing as being Indian, and meant they didn’t belong with anyone else.<br />  It was something Kami noticed, that she couldn’t help but notice: that she looked different from girls in pictures, girls on magazine covers, different from Angela and Holly and her own mother, who were all thin and pale and beautiful in what sometimes seemed to be the only right way. She noticed but tried not to mind, and didn’t mostly—just because she noticed didn’t mean she wanted to be someone else—but then she had met Jared and he hadn’t ever seemed to want to touch her. It was hard sometimes, not to be self-conscious.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “I wasn’t kidding. Someone really has to talk to her about her motivational speaking,” said Dad. “She’s meant to be the town leader, isn’t she?”<br />  “She’s the only adult sorcerer alive who isn’t strictly evil,” said Rusty. “So she wins the crown by default, I guess. Unless Henry wants it.”<br />  Kami supposed Henry was technically grown up, though he was only a couple of years older than Rusty.<br />  “Your town seems very nice,” said Henry, in the tones of one being very polite when offered a large unwanted present that was on fire. “But I only just got here. I don’t feel qualified to lead.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “About the last thing I said yesterday,” Jared said. “I’m sorry, and I didn’t mean to upset you. I was just surprised. I didn’t realize you thought about it that way.”<br />  “Okay, thanks for that,” said Kami, and began to walk determinedly down the passage away from him.<br />  “Kami,” Jared said behind her. “I’m—I’m honored that you did.”<br />  Which was not, Kami noted, “Let’s be together, then.” It was one of those nonsense things that people said, like “It’s not you, it’s me” and “You’re too good for me.” It meant, “I would like to very politely and very swiftly escape this relationship, like a Victorian gentleman in a rocket.”<br /><br />***<br />  “You’re great and smart and beautiful and amazing,” she announced. “If he doesn’t like you, he’s an idiot.”<br />  Holly blinked. “He?” she asked, and shook the hair back from her face.<br />  Kami blinked back. They sat blinking at each other, like a pair of bemused owls.<br />  “Is it …,” Kami said very slowly. “Is it … not a he?”<br />  Holly’s hands clenched on the book. For a long moment, Kami thought she had got this absolutely wrong, but then, even more slowly than Kami had spoken, Holly nodded.<br />  Kami launched herself at Holly, trying to hug her and hit her on the arm and let out a triumphant war cry all at once. She almost punched Holly in the chest but stopped herself at the last moment.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  She reached out and touched his face, the line of her cool hand against his scar. He had his back to the headboard already; he wasn’t sure how to get away from her without making it obvious.<br />  “I think you believe that you might destroy anything you touch,” Aunt Lillian said. “Give yourself more credit. You’re a Lynburn. I believe that you will only destroy that which you mean to destroy.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “We have some important stuff already,” Ash offered tentatively.<br />  Lillian frowned. “What do you mean?”<br />  Jared surrendered himself to the strangeness of this situation, sank back onto the pillows himself with his head near Lillian’s hip, and sighed heavily to attract his aunt’s attention. “He wants to know you love him more than that stupid house.”<br />  “It is a very nice house,” Aunt Lillian said, sounding offended. “Your ancestors are buried in the crypt of that house.”<br />  “Sure. Okay. We’ll get our lovely creepy house back. When they bury me in that crypt, I want ‘Jared, very inbred, deeply uncomfortable about it’ on my tombstone.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />He had found somewhere he did not fit but could belong anyway, and thought perhaps that meant family.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  Ash seemed alarmed to have been so firmly taken possession of by an eight-year-old. He and Tomo fell back a little, until they were walking with Jared and Kami.<br />  “I am so sad about my underwear,” Kami announced, and Ash looked as if he regretted all of his life decisions.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “How are things going with young what’s-his-face?” Angela asked, in what for Angela was conciliatory fashion, which of course meant not very conciliatory at all. “You know the one. Blond. Scowly. Bad attitude, which I have some sympathy for. Sloppy dresser, which I have no sympathy for at all.”<br />  “Also a terrible driver,” Kami said. “Wild about the eyes. Daddy issues so numerous the issues may be compiled into a book called <i>Who’s the Daddy? Both Options Are Evil.</i>”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “Now that you know that I’m not at all interested in Jared, is it inappropriate to say that I did get the impression that he might channel all those simmering repressed emotions in a useful way? I mean being explosively good in bed.”<br />  “Viking tiger in the sack, I have no doubt,” Kami said lightly, and felt a blush stage a hostile takeover of her neck and march up to claim the territory of her face.<br /><br />***<br /><br />The first thing to do was slip away from her father, who might have questions about why she kept insisting on going back to the lair of ultimate evil. Kami saw why so many teenagers who had adventures in books were interestingly tragic orphans. Parents were a real buzzkill, adventure-wise.<br /><br />[NOTE: One of my least favourite YA tropes. I like that the book calls it out, BUT Brennan is also guilty of doing the same damn thing, w/ Angela and Rusty's conveniently-missing parents letting them live on their own. I saw an earlier review speculate that the Montgomerys must be elite trained witch-hunters, what with their being trained in martial arts &amp; left on their own all the time -- and now I'm just sad and disappointed that that wasn't the case after all.]<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “I realize you are attempting to be humorous,” said Lillian, after a pause during which she stared some more. “I don’t understand it.”<br />  “Hey, you’re not the only family with a legacy. ‘Glass’ rhymes with ‘sass.’ Have you met my dad?”<br />  “I have had that dubious pleasure,” said Lillian. “He is, in fact, meant to be meeting me in order to, and I quote, ‘teach me to integrate better with society, display leadership skills, win over the populace, and stop acting like a robot princess from space.’ I admit that the humor in his humor escapes me as well.” She paused and suddenly looked determined. “I’m going to start without him.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “You two are getting on well these days,” she said lightly instead.<br />  “Bros before hoes,” said Jared. “By which of course I mean gardening tools, because I hold all the fine ladies of Sorry-in-the-Vale in the highest regard.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “Young Jared was standing at the door and he was wet to the skin. He has a look about him sometimes, like a stray dog that has been kicked too many times and has gone all the way past snarling and biting until all it does is shiver, waiting for the next kick. They’re almost patient about their misery, creatures like that, and they look at you with such eyes, beseeching you to make it all stop but not—not hoping that you will. It’s like they know you won’t, that the world isn’t going to be kind to them. Do you know what I mean?”<br />  “I know,” said Kami.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  Dad was giving Lillian very firm instructions on how to ask after people’s health, and ask how life was treating them, and how their jobs were going and their children were getting on.<br />  “I fail to see the point of all these questions,” Lillian told him in acid tones.<br />  “These questions are going to show that you have basic consideration for others, Lilliput. Such a thing will come as a surprise to many, but with luck it will be a nice surprise.”<br />  “If I show consideration for others,” Lillian Lynburn said grumpily, “will you tell me again about how you shot my husband?”<br />  Jon rolled his eyes. “Yes, Leigh, if you manage to approximate human behavior for half an hour, I will tell you your favorite story again.”<br />  Lillian propped her chin on her hand, looked smug, and bestowed a smile on old Roger Stearn as he went past. He looked briefly dazzled, but that might have been his cataracts.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “It’s clear what the girl meant,” said Lillian. “She meant a specific ‘them.’ She meant my boys. Of course Rob wants to lure my boys onto his side. They have to be protected—they can’t do magic and are utterly helpless and vulnerable.”<br />  “That’s so true,” said Jared, folding his arms so the sleeves of his T-shirt strained and fluttering his eyelashes. “Please save me, Aunt Lillian.”<br />  “I realize you are making another effort to be humorous,” said Lillian, patting his arm, “and I wish you would stop. But of course I will save you.”<br /><br />***<br /><br />  She took Kami’s wrist and turned it so that her hand lay palm up. In it she placed a curved shell. Kami felt the ridges of the shell’s surface against her skin and glimpsed the pearlescent curling cave within.<br />  “You can hear the sound of the sea in these shells,” said Lillian. “So you can hear the sound of a sorcerer’s voice. If I need you, I can call to you through the shell. If you need me, do the same.”<br />  “Okay,” Kami said slowly. “Thanks very much for this artifact of wondrous magic. I have a small suggestion, though. I’d like you to give me what my people call a ‘phone number.’ And I will give you mine in exchange. You can also have my dad’s and Angela’s and Rusty’s.”<br />  “I do not want anybody’s phone number,” said Lillian, flushing slightly.<br />  She turned and went back downstairs, toward the sound of Dad’s and Martha Wright’s voices. Kami slipped the shell in her pocket.<br />  “That lady is a weirdo,” Tomo observed.<br />  “You’re an astute judge of character, Tomo,” said Kami.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “Would you do me a favor?” asked Mr. Glass. Holly blinked, stunned, and he went on, “Would you watch the boys for me? Let me sit with Angela for a bit.”<br />  He looked at her the way kind teachers had sometimes looked at Holly, when she had given them a piece of homework she thought she had done all right with and was waiting around to maybe hear them say so. Holly felt pathetic again—she was seventeen years old, someone had died, and she was still hanging around hoping for an adult to call her a good girl.<br />  “You’re a brave girl,” said Mr. Glass instead, and Holly would have done anything he wanted.<br /><br />***<br /><br />  “So you do …” Still, after all this, Jared hesitated, hardly daring to believe. “Do you love me?”<br />  Kami tipped back her head and laughed at him, felt her laugh running along his bones, delight mirrored back to her and back again. The sun hung above them like a silent shining bell in the sky. She opened up her thoughts and let him see it all, the story of her love laid out before him as though written in scarlet and gold.<br />  She said: <i>Read my mind.</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="5007717861708042406" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_779162981" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/779162981" />
    <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"><img alt=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467844p2/703854.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/779162981?book_show_action=true">Dec 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"> ♥ Rebecca ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780375870439" href="/book/show/20342504-unmade">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=my-heroine">my-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer779162981" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1904359468276948966">This review can also be found on my blog: <a href='http://amatchmadeinheavenreviews.blogspot.ca/2014/11/unmade-by-sarah-rees-brennan-lynburn.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Match Made in Heaven</a><br/><br/>This series is one of my absolute favourites. 5-stars across the board. Its just so unique. I really cant get over how unusual it was. Its so dark. And by dark I mean <i>dark</i>. The bad guys in this story are true evil. There is so much blood and death and destruction and pure greed and <i>evil</i>. Yet, at the same time, Kami is simply one of the best, smartest, funniest, and wittiest YA heroines I have ever read. She provides a balance that y</span>
  <span id="freeText1904359468276948966" style="display:none">This review can also be found on my blog: <a href="http://amatchmadeinheavenreviews.blogspot.ca/2014/11/unmade-by-sarah-rees-brennan-lynburn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">A Match Made in Heaven</a><br /><br />This series is one of my absolute favourites. 5-stars across the board. Its just so unique. I really cant get over how unusual it was. Its so dark. And by dark I mean <i>dark</i>. The bad guys in this story are true evil. There is so much blood and death and destruction and pure greed and <i>evil</i>. Yet, at the same time, Kami is simply one of the best, smartest, funniest, and wittiest YA heroines I have ever read. She provides a balance that you need in order to handle all the darkness. This is one of those books where, when you try to list your favourites quotes, you find that you want to quote the whole book. <br /><br />Another thing I loved about this book was all the love. Kami and Jared's love is epic, but it wasn't the only focus. Everyone loved each other and were willing to sacrifice so much for each other. Kami loved Jared, but she also loved Ash and Rusty, in a different way. She never really gave her love for them a title, but it was probably more brotherly. Then of course she loved Angela and Holly, and her brothers and her parents, and everything she did was for them. If you have read this series, then you know exactly how much Rusty loved Angela and Kami. How much Angela loved Kami, and Rusty, and Holly. How much Jared loved Ash, and Holly, and Lillian. How much Lillian loved Ash and Jared. And how much Ash loved Jared, Lillian, and Kami. They forged such a large family together, through everything that they went through they became stronger. <br /><br />As much as I love Kami and Jared's oddly epic love story, its really everyone in this series that make me love it so much. All the characters, the way they fight for each other and what is right and what they believe in. The way that they handle the tragedies in their lives. How they never quit, they hang on to what they have and keep going. How they always look for the bright side, and even when they believe that they are all going to die, they still do what needs to be done. Despite the evil of the story, and the heartbreaking deaths, this series was so uplifting and inspiring because of the courage of Kami and her friends and family. I will never forget it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1904359468276948966" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1306666635" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1306666635" />
    <a title="Vippi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/28376061-vippi"><img alt="Vippi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394115271p2/28376061.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1306666635?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vippi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vippi" href="/user/show/28376061-vippi">Vippi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1306666635" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17360601646506505645">Overall series: ★★★★<br/>Unmade: ★★★ 1/2<br/><br/>Okay, mourning-time is finished. Let’s review this one.<br/><br/>I loved this series and it characters (well, Kami is fantastic, isn’t she?... and her dad and Rusty <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[*still crying* <a class='jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction'>(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, too). So when I finally picked up Unmade I had great expectations.<br/><br/>I can’t say I didn’t like it. As the previous instalments, Unmade was a humorous, adventure-packed reading … but… some elements disappointed me a little bit:<br/><br/>-	<u>too much angst</u>: angst was the key-word</span>
  <span id="freeText17360601646506505645" style="display:none">Overall series: ★★★★<br />Unmade: ★★★ 1/2<br /><br />Okay, mourning-time is finished. Let’s review this one.<br /><br />I loved this series and it characters (well, Kami is fantastic, isn’t she?... and her dad and Rusty <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[*still crying* <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, too). So when I finally picked up Unmade I had great expectations.<br /><br />I can’t say I didn’t like it. As the previous instalments, Unmade was a humorous, adventure-packed reading … but… some elements disappointed me a little bit:<br /><br />-	<u>too much angst</u>: angst was the key-word in the relationship between Kami and Jared, but IMO the Author pushed it too far here. All that back and forth game between them annoyed me and at times I wanted to shout: “Jared, it’s so clear that Kami loves you. So, please, put an end to being such a moron and tell her that you love her too!”;<br /><br />-	<u>Rob Lyburn and his evil sorcerers</u>: the antagonists’ wait-and-see policy didn’t entirely convince me. They passed too much time temporize, without seriously dealing with the threat represented by Kami’s gang;<br /><br />-	<u>
  <b>“The crash”</b>
</u>: I knew that I would have suffered, but I wasn’t prepared to such a tragedy. I didn’t complain about that cruel, sadistic underhanded trick in itself. <b>What really made it unbearable was that it was unnecessary to the story</b>. So, Mrs. Breannan, why are you so merciless?<br /><br />All in all, despite the misgivings my broken heart has pointed out, <b>I can’t help recommending this series</b>. It’s worth reading it. <br />Just make sure you have enough Kleenex at hand.</span>

    <a title="Cody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/35007929-cody"><img alt="Cody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415626292p2/35007929.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1184140928?book_show_action=true">Jan 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cody" href="/user/show/35007929-cody">Cody</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1184140928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18408197761239814670"><b>"Which is it going to be sorcerer? Drown or burn?"</b><br/><br/><u>The Lynburn Legacy is over.</u><br/><br/>I was actually a little sad to see this end now that I’ve finished Unmade. The series was by no means perfect and had its faults along the way but they didn’t take away from the story or the sensational characters that carry these books, I really enjoyed them.<br/><br/>The conclusion to this series is filled with action, drama, sacrifices, unrequited love and soo many plot twists. I hated the way Untold ended as usual Brennan pro</span>
  <span id="freeText18408197761239814670" style="display:none"><b>"Which is it going to be sorcerer? Drown or burn?"</b><br /><br /><u>The Lynburn Legacy is over.</u><br /><br />I was actually a little sad to see this end now that I’ve finished Unmade. The series was by no means perfect and had its faults along the way but they didn’t take away from the story or the sensational characters that carry these books, I really enjoyed them.<br /><br />The conclusion to this series is filled with action, drama, sacrifices, unrequited love and soo many plot twists. I hated the way Untold ended as usual Brennan provided a killer cliffhanger so I was delighted that Unmade made quick work of rectifying this, YAY JARED!<br /><br />So Rob Lynburn has proven time and time again that he is the most crazy and power-hungry Lynburn that has ever existed, I didn’t think he could get worse but I was so so wrong. He wants revenge against the town members who will not submit to his rule and he attacks and destroys what they treasure most. In order to stop Rob’s plans in Untold, Kami become Ash’s source and now in Unmade they have to plan to save the town and cope with their intimate magical bond.<br /><br />I have mainly rated these books on the characters and this remains for Unmade. I was so glad we got to see more of Lillian Lynburn and Jon Glass and if I’m honest I thought it was going somewhere between the two but alas this didn’t happen. The loss of one of the most loved characters was heart breaking and the development of romance between Angie &amp; Holly was wonderfully told. I felt the romance between Kami &amp; Jared was a little dragged and was frustrating but nowhere near as frustrating as when Ash was involved.<br /><br />The final book provides a lot of twists and turns that will keep you interested but I dare say without these the story would have fell a little flat with the slow pace. I wasn’t too happy with the ending but I was happy that we actually found out what happened in the end.. <i>I hate it when books leave you guessing!!!</i><br /><br />Overall I have really enjoyed the series so if you want to read a fresh unique series with crazy cliffhangers and loveable characters then this is definitely for you.<br /><br /><a href="http://literary-lyobsessed.blogspot.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Literary-ly Obsessed</a></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JAIME" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JAIME" href="/user/show/31366847-jaime">JAIME</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10311892529646729112">There was an event in this that made me cry - A LOT. But, otherwise it was fairly unremarkable. Not bad, but didn't blow my socks off for the final book in a trilogy. <br/><br/>The love triangle, that wasn't really a love triangle and the constant on again off again relationship off our protagonist through all three books, really put a dampener on things for me. <br/><br/>Still, an overall enjoyable series. </span>
